Ground Truth: Based on the search results, here are the instructions related to the use of the imaging oil with part number D9U80A:\n\n### Instructions for Using Imaging Oil (P/N D9U80A)\n\n#### Prerequisites:\n- Ensure that the press software version 10081.0.0.180 I-Fix3.i17 is installed and active on the digital press.\n- You will need six gallons of imaging oil (P/N D9U80A), three gallons per color.\n\n#### Steps to Install the PFAS-Free Cyan and Yellow Plugin:\n1. **Shut Down Press Software:**\n   - Shut down the press software but keep the computer on.\n2. **Check for Updates:**\n   - From HP Indigo Radar, click \'Check for Updates\' and then install the 10081.0.0.180 I-Fix3 PFAS Free CYAN and YELLOW Plugin.\n3. **Start Press Software:**\n   - Start the press software.\n4. **Drain and Clean Ink Stations:**\n   - Drain and clean the cyan and yellow ink stations.\n5. **Fill Ink Stations:**\n   - Fill the cyan and yellow ink stations with fresh imaging oil (P/N D9U80A).\n6. **Rebuild Inks:**\n   - Rebuild cyan and yellow inks using the Color Change wizard and import new cyan and yellow ink files.\n\n#### Steps to Uninstall the PFAS-Free Cyan and Yellow Plugin:\n1. **Shut Down Press Software:**\n   - Shut down the press software.\n2. **Remove Plugin:**\n   - In Windows, click the Start button.\n   - Scroll to the HP Indigo Digital Press folder.\n   - Below the folder, click \'Remove Repair 60586_Cyan_and_yellow_optimization_Plug-in\' and follow the on-screen uninstall instructions.\n3. **Start Press Software:**\n   - Start the press software.\n4. **Ink and BID Settings:**\n   - While in Standby mode, click Main menu > Ink and BID.\n   - In the Ink and BID window that appears, click Ink Settings.\n   - In the Ink Settings window that appears, select the Ink Files tab at the left.\n   - Click Import and import the Cyan ink file by selecting it and clicking OK.\n\n### References:\n1. [PFAS-Free Cyan and Yellow Plugin TN-2648](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210300) - Page 2\n2. User Input:  actual print size/ image size
Ground Truth: The actual print size or image size for HP Indigo presses can vary depending on the specific model and configuration. Here are some details for the HP Indigo V12 Digital Press:\n\n1. **Image Size**:\n   - The image size for the HP Indigo V12 Digital Press is 322 mm x 5330 mm (12.68 in x 209.84 in) ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210864), page 7).\n   - At a later stage of product development, the image size will be 324 mm x 5330 mm (12.76 in x 209.84 in) ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210864), page 7).\n\n2. **Image Width**:\n   - The image width ranges from 196 mm to 322 mm ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210864), page 7).\n   - At a later stage of product development, the image width will range from 196 mm to 324 mm ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210864), page 7).\n\n3. **Repeat Length**:\n   - The repeat length for the HP Indigo V12 Digital Press can be manually set or adjusted based on the job. It allows for the adjustment of the gap between sheets, which is essential for optimizing substrate usage ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/393447), page 168).\n\n4. **Image Resolution**:\n   - The image resolution for the HP Indigo V12 Digital Press is 800 DPI ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210864), page 23).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Product Release Content Review - V12, HP Indigo Ltd., [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/210864), page 7.\n2. HP Production Pro for Commercial - User Guide, HP Indigo Ltd., [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/393447), page 168.

CA494-14600. Flexible packaging development also involves considerations for sustainabi lity and applicable environmental\nand recycling regulations.\nSustainability\nFlexible packaging has ma ny sustainable advantages:\n● Reduced waste volume — Creation of flexible packaging u ses fewer natural resources; improvements\nin production processes have reduced water and en ergy consumption, greenh ouse gas emissions, and\nvolatile organic compounds. All this results in producing less waste and greatly reducing landfill\ndiscards.\n● Reduced package storage volume and freight costs  — With flexible packaging, converters,\nmanufacturers, shippers, and warehouse personnel ga in more cost-efficient production and handling.\n● Reduced package weight — Lighter-weight flexible packaging r esults in less transportation-related\nenergy and fossil fuel consumption and environmental pollution. Reduci ng package weight in transport\nreduces actual fuel use. Greater fu el efficiency in transportation cost s reduces fossil fuel consumption.\nPackage life cycle\nThe life cycle of a typical package compr ises the following steps and elements:\nFigure 2-2   Package life cycle\n● Package engineering  — Conducted by the packer  (normally the brand owne r) to decide how the\npackage will look on the shelf, what it will contain, its size and materials type.\n● Graphic design  — The art designer  (on behalf of the brand and in  cooperation with  the converter)\nprepares the package form, graphics positioning, bran ding, use instructions.\n● Pre-press  — At the converter  site, the graphic file is transferred to a ready-to-print file including color\nseparations, screen angles and ty pes, imposition, trapping, etc.\n● Printing tools  — The converter  prepares the image carrier (plate s or cylinders, depending on the\nprinting technology) and fits  it to the printing press.\nENWW Package life cycle 3'), Document(metadata={'ratingResponse': {'number_of_votes': 0, 'rating': 0.0}, 'persona': 'Operator', 'format': 'pdf', 'description': ' CA494-09370', 'language': 'en', 'title': 'SMS Designer for InDesign CC 2020 User Guide', 'uuid': '07403185-c87f-45e1-b1b6-9891d046df62', 'products': [], 'ti_desc_prod': 'SMS Designer for InDesign CC 2020 User Guide  CA494-09370', 'page_number': 179, 'provider': 'Storage-Service', 'contentUpdateDate': '2023-07-23 10:10:56', 'catalog_number': 'CA494-09370', 'asset_state': {'numericOrder': 99, 'dueDate': None, 'name': 'Regular'}, 'namedAsset': '07403185-c87f-45e1-b1b6-9891d046df62', 'lowestRolesList': 'Press Operator', 'renderLink': 'https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/48083', 'publisher': {'name': 'HP Indigo', 'id': 1}, 'documentID': '48083', 'Domain': 'Indigo', 'Doc_Status': 'published', 'contentType': 'Document'}, page_content='SMS Designer for InDesign CC 2020 User Guide  CA494-09370. User Input:  its for cleaning bid roller and replacing bid base
Ground Truth: To clean the BID roller and replace the BID base, follow these steps:\n\n### Cleaning the BID Roller\n\n1. **Remove the BID from the Press**:\n   - Pull out the specific BID from the press and keep it on the slider ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 1).\n\n2. **Remove the Developer Roller**:\n   - Remove the developer roller from the BID base and place it on the stand ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 1).\n\n3. **Insert the Cleaning Jig**:\n   - Carefully insert the cleaning jig between the BID electrodes ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 2).\n\n4. **Clean the BID Base Electrode**:\n   - Pull the jig from one side of the BID base to the other side.\n   - Clean the BID base electrode using a lint-free wipe soaked with imaging oil to remove any particles or residual ink on the electrodes ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 2).\n\n5. **Clean the Developer Roller**:\n   - Wipe the developer roller using a lint-free wipe soaked with imaging oil to remove any particles from the roller ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 2).\n\n6. **Reassemble the Developer Roller**:\n   - Reassemble the developer roller onto the BID base ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 2).\n\n### Replacing the BID Base\n\n1. **Slide Out the BID Base**:\n   - During this procedure, slide out only one BID at a time ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_10912658-9704708-16), page 1).\n\n2. **Install the BID Developer Roller**:\n   - Install the BID developer roller ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_10912658-9704708-16), page 1).\n\n3. **Wet the Shape Seal with Imaging Oil**:\n   - Wet the shape seal with imaging oil ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_10912658-9704708-16), page 1).\n\n4. **Install the BID Developer**:\n   - Install the BID developer. Be careful not to damage the OPE ring ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_10912658-9704708-16), page 1).\n\n5. **Replace the Lower Sponge Roller**:\n   - Replace the lower sponge roller. Wet the sponges with imaging oil ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_10912658-9704708-16), page 1).\n\n6. **Reinsert the BID into the Press**:\n   - Reinsert the BID into the press and continue printing ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 2).\n\n### Sources List\n1. New Concept BID TN-2383, HP Indigo, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47272), page 2.\n2. Installing the binary ink developers (BIDs), HP Indigo, [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_10912658-9704708-16), page 1.\n3. BID Particle Cleaning Jig Ser4 TN-2380, HP Indigo, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47270), page 1.

User Input:  PLC reset
Ground Truth: To perform a PLC reset on an HP Indigo press, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Preparation**:\n   - Before any PLC reset, perform the washing cycle to the priming unwinder, allowing it to finish and only then performing the PLC reset ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9192062_en-US-4), page 9).\n   - If a message appears regarding a washing cycle or washing liquid problem, replace with cleaning water and reset the washing counter ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9192062_en-US-4), page 9).\n\n2. **Performing the Reset**:\n   - If the PE2 PLC shows an error, it might be related to PE2 FE safety parameters. Reset CB21 on PE2 for 15 seconds to restart the drive. Confirm that FE parameter 17.23 node is 5 ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669), page 269).\n   - Confirm that PE2 FE address is 192.168.101.50. If not, follow these steps:\n     - Turn off CB21 on PE1.\n     - Ping 192.168.101.12 to ensure the communication works.\n     - Flash PE2 FE with the 192.168.101.12 address.\n     - Turn on CB21 on PE1.\n     - Confirm that PE2 FE address is 192.168.101.50 ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669), page 269).\n   - Confirm that parameter 3.36 is set to 8U. If not, change it to 1000 and save ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669), page 269).\n   - Shut down the press and turn it back on ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669), page 269).\n\n3. **Post-Reset**:\n   - If the controller was replaced or reset to the factory setup (1233), change parameter 3.36 to 8 and save with 1000. Restart the controller ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669), page 269).\n   - Make sure the safety parameter value is 8 for all Digitax units (except the BCS Digitax). For the BCS Digitax, make sure the safety parameter value is 5 and save with 1001 ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669), page 269).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Best Practice Guide for HP Indigo 20000 Digital Press, page 9, [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9192062_en-US-4).\n2. Installation Manual for HP Indigo 8K Digital Press, page 269, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64669).

User Input:  How to use refine color function on Indigo 7900
Ground Truth: To use the Refine Color function on the HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Access the Color Calibration Wizard**:\n   - Navigate to the Main Menu.\n   - Select `Print Quality`.\n   - Choose `Color Calibration Wizard` ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918), page 154).\n\n2. **Set Up the Paper**:\n   - In the initial window, set the paper to `Max Paper (300gsm)` ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918), page 154).\n\n3. **Calibration Type and Settings**:\n   - In the Start window, set the Calibration type and How to run settings as required ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918), page 154).\n\n4. **Perform Full Color Calibration**:\n   - Follow the wizard instructions to perform the full color calibration ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918), page 169).\n\n5. **Define Media Fingerprint**:\n   - Go to `Print Preferences > Color Calibration tab`.\n   - Define new substrate properties under the `More` tab.\n   - Run Media Fingerprint by defining a new substrate with the Media Fingerprint activated and then perform Color Calibration ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918), page 169).\n\n6. **Check Optical Density**:\n   - Use an X-Rite densitometer to check the optical density of the solid squares and ensure they meet the required specifications ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918), page 158).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Installation - HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press, page 154, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918)\n2. Installation - HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press, page 169, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918)\n3. Installation - HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press, page 158, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918)

User Input:  ts steps
Ground Truth: Based on the documents retrieved, here are the steps for troubleshooting and servicing the spectrophotometer (SPM) for the HP Indigo WS6600 and WS6800 Digital Presses:\n\n1. **Self-Calibration Failure**:\n   - If the press prints FCC and passes but gives a self-calibration failure, follow the self-calibration TS steps in the document \'CA393-09670 - Spectrophotometer Servicing and Troubleshooting\' (page 45) ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27896)).\n\n2. **SPM Self-Calibration**:\n   - If the SPM self-calibration is failing, ensure the press passes the Z and X axis test.\n   - Follow the self-calibration TS steps in the UI Error: Spectrophotometer self-calibration failed. This may affect color accuracy, specifically steps 7–13.\n   - Check the SPM highest setup, as described in Figure 1.\n   - Ensure the SPM nut holding the ceramic tile in place is not loose ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9124823-8898532-16)).\n\n3. **Replacing the Temperature Sensor on the ITC Reservoir**:\n   - The temperature sensor is on the right wall of the ITC reservoir.\n   - Disconnect the sensor electrical cable from its connector.\n   - Disconnect the sensor using a 22mm open wrench.\n   - Replace the temperature sensor with a new unit ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_8703851-8699692-16)).\n\n4. **Replacing the Liquid Level Sensor on the ITC Reservoir**:\n   - Follow the steps to replace the liquid level sensor on the ITC reservoir ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_8703848_en-US-4)).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Spectrophotometer (SPM) Servicing and Troubleshooting, CA393-09670, HP Indigo, [link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27896), page 95.\n2. SPM self-calibration is failing, HP Indigo, [link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9124823-8898532-16), page 1.\n3. Replacing the temperature sensor on the ITC reservoir, HP Indigo, [link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_8703851-8699692-16), page 1.\n4. 15K/35K/18K Utility Cabinet Service, HP Indigo, [link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_8703848_en-US-4), page 50.

User Input:  ho to change feeder drawer cable
Ground Truth: To change the feeder drawer cable on an HP Indigo press, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Turn on the Feeder Power**:\n   - Turn on the feeder power and use the button on the front panel to lower the drawers.\n   - Turn off the feeder power.\n\n2. **Remove the Feeder Covers**:\n   - Remove the feeder input side cover to expose the side of the drawer and reach the cables conduit.\n   - Remove the rear cover of the feeder to reach the drawer board.\n\n3. **Open the Drawer and Disconnect the Cables**:\n   - Open the drawer and disconnect the cables from the drawer connectors panel (Figure 4-33) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601).\n\n4. **Remove the Cables Conduit**:\n   - With an Allen key (size 3), remove the 4 screws that attach the cables conduit to the drawer side.\n   - Remove the 2 screws at the head (near the connectors panel). The screws are under the wires, so move them aside/apart to reach the screws.\n\n5. **Install the New Cables Conduit**:\n   - Start inserting the new cables conduit from the open drawer side and spread it to its full length along the side of the drawer (Figure 4-47) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601).\n\n6. **Reconnect the Cables**:\n   - Reconnect the cables to the drawer connectors panel and ensure they are properly secured.\n\n7. **Secure the Cables**:\n   - Tie-wrap the cables into a bundle and attach them to the bottom and/or side of the drawer as relevant (Figure 4-63) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601).\n\n8. **Reassemble the Feeder**:\n   - Reattach the feeder covers and ensure everything is properly secured.\n\n### Sources:\n1. Feeder service instructions for the HP Indigo feeder. CA393-07310, HP Indigo 7800 Digital Press — feeder drawer service, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601), page 73.\n2. Feeder service instructions for the HP Indigo feeder. CA393-07310, HP Indigo 7800 Digital Press — feeder drawer service, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601), page 80.\n3. Feeder service instructions for the HP Indigo feeder. CA393-07310, HP Indigo 7800 Digital Press — feeder drawer service, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601), page 84.\n4. Feeder service instructions for the HP Indigo feeder. CA393-07310, HP Indigo 7800 Digital Press — feeder drawer service, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19601), page 90.

User Input:  diagram for the imaging oil route on HP 12000
Ground Truth: Here is the information regarding the imaging oil route for the HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press:\n\n1. **Filling the Imaging Oil Reservoir**:\n   - Pour imaging oil into the clean reservoir and the dirty reservoir.\n   - The total amount of imaging oil in the entire reservoir should be 40 L (10.5 gallons).\n   - Refer to Figure 6-1 for the imaging oil reservoir diagram.\n   - [Source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066) (HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 160).\n\n2. **Pouring Imaging Oil into the Ink Tank**:\n   - Pour 10 L (2.5 gallons) of imaging oil into the ink tank.\n   - Refer to Figure 6-5 for the imaging oil diagram.\n   - [Source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066) (HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 168).\n\n3. **Filling the Buffer Chamber**:\n   - Pour 30 L (8 bottles) of imaging oil into the imaging oil inlet to fill the buffer chamber.\n   - Install the two waste bottles.\n   - Refer to Figure 6-8 for the waste bottles diagram.\n   - [Source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066) (HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 170).\n\n4. **Wetting the Shape Seal with Imaging Oil**:\n   - Wet the shape seal with imaging oil.\n   - Refer to Figure 9-4 for the wetting shape seal diagram.\n   - [Source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066) (HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 206).\n\n### Sources:\n1. HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 160, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066)\n2. HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 168, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066)\n3. HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 170, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066)\n4. HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, Page 206, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066)\n\nThese references should provide you with the detailed diagrams and steps for the imaging oil route on the HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press.

User Input:  Recommended ink tank rebuild intervals for HP Indigo 12000
Ground Truth: The recommended ink tank rebuild intervals for the HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press involve several maintenance procedures, including replacing and cleaning the ink tank filter, cleaning the level sensor (LCS) board, and the ink optical density sensor (ODS). Here are the detailed steps:\n\n1. **Replacing the Ink Tank Filter**:\n   - Wear latex gloves, safety goggles, and a lab coat before beginning the procedures.\n   - Access the ink cabinet (IC) and disconnect the ink tank tubes.\n   - Open the ink tank and remove the ink pump top assembly.\n   - Reinsert the ink pump top assembly into the ink tank.\n   - Close the ink tank and IC cabinet door ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9057250_en-US-6), page 30).\n\n2. **Cleaning the Ink Tank Filter and Level Sensor (LCS) Board**:\n   - View the video \'Cleaning The Ink Tank Filter\' available in the PrintOS Knowledge Zone ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29417)).\n   - Wear latex gloves, safety goggles, and a lab coat before beginning the procedures.\n   - Use special jigs and tools such as an air duster or air pressure pistol (lower than 1.5 bar), a set of Allen keys, lint-free wipes, and an imaging oil bottle ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9057250_en-US-6), page 37).\n\n3. **Cleaning the Ink Optical Density Sensor (ODS)**:\n   - Wear latex gloves, safety goggles, and a lab coat before beginning the procedures.\n   - Use the same special jigs and tools as mentioned above ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9057250_en-US-6), page 36).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Ink Cabinet Service — CA493-00400 Rev 08, HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press, [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9057250_en-US-6), pages 30, 36, 37.\n2. HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Installation Manual, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33066), pages 167, 168.

User Input:  spot color alias
Ground Truth: ### Spot Color Alias in HP Indigo Presses\n\n#### Overview\nSpot color aliasing is a feature in HP Indigo presses that allows users to create and maintain custom tables of spot colors and their desired separation values. This is particularly useful for ensuring color consistency and accuracy in print jobs.\n\n#### Working with Spot Color Tables\nSpot color tables allow users to define custom spot colors and their separation values. These tables can be managed through the web client and are selected in the job ticket for a particular print job. The following features are supported:\n\n1. **Creating a New Spot Color Table**:\n   - To create a new spot color table, navigate to the System tab, expand Resources in the Navigation Panel, and click on Spot Color Tables.\n   - Click on \'New\', type a name for the new spot color table, and then click \'Save\'.\n\n2. **Importing a Spot Color Table**:\n   - To import a spot color table, click on \'Import\', browse to locate the .csv file to import, and then click \'Open\'.\n   - Note: The imported .csv file must match the formatting requirements for spot color tables. The name of the table in the .csv file is used as the name of the imported spot color table.\n\n3. **Editing a Spot Color Table**:\n   - To edit a spot color table, select a spot color table entry in the list, and then click \'Edit\'.\n   - Make the necessary edits to the color table, and then click \'Save\'.\n\n4. **Duplicating a Spot Color Table**:\n   - To duplicate a spot color table, select a spot color table entry in the list, and then click \'Duplicate\'.\n   - Type a name for the new spot color table, and then click \'Save\'.\n\n5. **Exporting a Spot Color Table**:\n   - To export a spot color table, select a spot color table entry in the list, and then click \'Export\'.\n   - A CSV file containing the spot color table definition is immediately made available for download through the web client.\n\n#### Important Notes\n- Each custom spot color table defines a set of required separations. The job can define additional separations not in the table, but a job fails if one or more of the separations in the table is not defined in the job.\n- In the custom spot color interface, special recognized separation names are represented with the appropriate color dot. Other separation names are represented with a gray star.\n- To avoid conflicting operations, do not simultaneously edit a spot color table in multiple browser sessions.\n\n#### References\n- [HP Production Pro for Commercial - User Guide](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/393447), Page 81\n- [HP Production Pro for Labels and Packaging - User Guide](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/393448), Page 98\n\n### Sources List\n1. HP Production Pro for Commercial - User Guide, Page 81, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/393447)\n2. HP Production Pro for Labels and Packaging - User Guide, Page 98, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/393448)

User Input:  Feed head removal and replacement 
Ground Truth: To remove and replace the feed head on an HP Indigo press, follow these steps:\n\n### Prerequisites:\n1. **Power Off the Machine**: Ensure the machine is powered off before starting the procedure.\n\n### Removal:\n1. **Open the Drawer**: \n   - Completely open the drawer (Fig. 2).\n   - Remove the stop from the middle slide guide and push it into the feeder (Fig. 3).\n\n2. **Remove the Feed Head**:\n   - Open the drawer completely.\n   - Remove the screw.\n   - Pull the feed head.\n   - Disconnect the ultrasonic sensor.\n   - Remove the ultrasonic sensor with the screws and the washer.\n\n### Replacement:\n1. **Install the New Assembly**:\n   - Install the new feed head assembly in reverse order.\n   - Restore the machine to normal operating conditions.\n\nFor a detailed visual guide, you can refer to the video [here](https://signedurl.printos.com/amazon_genesis.production/be-storage-1483431-57475c6486-6hltv/d0db598d-5cfc-4182-9706-95fcd4b4946d/6a74fc3b-9551-43f8-ae42-7b5e89829ff3/S3+Feedhead+removal+and+replacement+v3.mp4?Expires=1735295113&Signature=cIEyFOM1yTcXTZAxHF45Drgbq85dCynKXN1axZ5Z9JAufPC3hMraF8Pxpz26gwguuCM-CxPDFICNjQ-U67MGjjaR2FOBU08gF2P3OHjvPxphUh7u02zLj3Ir60m9qITYmUXBvldBB3K9HcIFQyJe53UvY5DLYbtbTomeOXfZJd6YJVXJYA9GzhOhXntKuLHshp1pBbtG~6aRWvuFSw14KLnHeZvjEceqshk~xw202NlkDt126ps~bjvoPM5LkTDvWeCfl7qN8SsMlP~t2TPYHOLSMRb3fb7aFW8NMPg8ul80Y86Cv3GaL1Kc-s9aHDX6dOed4WoC0X4TsL74NSRL9Q__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAI6VBR2Q6NBVXHWDA).\n\n### Sources:\n1. **Feeder Part 7 - Pages 60-68**: [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/18086)\n2. **Feeder Part 5 - Pages 32-36**: [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/26369)\n3. **Feeder Part 11 - Pages 65-70**: [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/26342)\n4. **Feeder Part 3 - Pages 27-36**: [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/18002)

User Input:  Dynamic Prism
Ground Truth: The dynamic prism is a crucial component in HP Indigo presses, designed to improve registration by compensating for small and fast changes in press speed and angular position. Here are the detailed steps to test and troubleshoot the dynamic prism:\n\n### Testing the Dynamic Prism\n1. **Diagnostics Check:**\n   - Navigate to `Diagnostics > Writing Head > WH Elements` tab.\n   - Observe the range of the Prism compensation in the Max and Min fields in the Position window.\n   - If the range is greater than ±300, there is a serious mechanical problem or incorrect/unstable motor speed that needs to be corrected first.\n\n2. **Print Registration Job:**\n   - Print a few sheets of the `SBN_Registration` job and observe the registration.\n   - In the `Diagnostics > Writing Head > WH Elements` tab, force the dynamic prism position to 0.\n   - Ensure the hand icon is enabled (white). Click on the hand icon with the right mouse button to enable it.\n   - Print a few sheets of the `SBN_Registration` job again and observe the registration.\n   - If the registration is worse, the dynamic prism is functioning properly. Release the force.\n\n### Troubleshooting the Dynamic Prism\n1. **Check Controller Version:**\n   - In the `Options > Systab Editor > whif960ConfigTopic`, check the `dynamicPrismType`.\n   - It should be `HT_VER2`. If it is `HT_VER1`, try reinstalling the writing head from the floppy. If it remains `HT_VER1`, contact HP.\n\n2. **Check Connections:**\n   - Shut down the system and switch off the mains power supply and UPS.\n   - Remove the writing head cover.\n   - Check all cables and connections to ensure the dynamic prism control board is properly seated. Remove and reinstall the board if required.\n\n3. **Replace Components:**\n   - If necessary, replace the dynamic prism control board.\n   - Replace the electronic plate if required.\n\n### Additional Steps\n- **Toggle Dynamic Prism Position:**\n  - Force the dynamic prism to 300 and print the `SBN_Registration` job.\n  - During the run, the dynamic prism will revert to approximately 0.\n  - Toggle between the 0 position and the 300 position during the run by placing the cursor in the 300 field and pressing `<Enter>` multiple times.\n  - Observe the range of the dynamic prism compensation in the position window to ensure the toggle is working.\n\n- **Main Motor Control Troubleshooting:**\n  - In the `Options > Systab Editor > mainMotorTopic`, change the `baldorFullSpeedRpm` saved value to the default value.\n  - If there is an improvement in registration, there was a main motor speed problem.\n  - Print about 400 separations in one run. If the problem reappears, it may be due to scaling.\n  - In the `Options > Systab Editor > scalingParametersTopic`, change the `verticalScalingDirection` and `verticalUserScalingDirection` to `DIR_NONE`.\n  - Reset the `baldorFullSpeedRpm` saved value to the default value.\n\n### References\n- [HP Indigo Service Document Writing Head](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24932) (Page 45-47)\n- [Dynamic POS and Dynamic Mirror Technical Service](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9480701_en-US-6) (Page 5)\n- [HP Indigo Service Document Registration Troubleshooting](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/26621) (Page 13)\n\n### Sources List\n1. HP Indigo Service Document Writing Head, Page 45-47, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24932)\n2. Dynamic POS and Dynamic Mirror Technical Service, Page 5, [HP Indigo](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9480701_en-US-6)\n3. HP Indigo Service Document Registration Troubleshooting, Page 13, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/26621)

It occurs in \nconjunction with PIP-side misregistration before or after performing the wizard \ncorrection. \nThe problem appears only when printing an odd number of duplex sheets. Theory — DP POS — Dynamic mirror 2\nThis section explains the concept of dynamic mirror.\nDynamic Mirror\nThe following points explain about dynamic mirror (or prism)\n● An image is created on the PIP drum by the writing head.\n● The created separation is transferred to the blanket cylinder (ITM).\n● From the blanket cylinder, the separation is transferred to the substrate.\n● After the image is completed, the substrate moves out through the transport system to the stacker/\nexit unit.\n● All events and processes in the press affect the main motor speed by adding of removing a load to \nand from the system.\n● The press speed is controlled by the Baldor/Servostar controller driver, but the reaction time of the \ncontroller is relatively slow when compensating for speed.\n● The dynamic prism (or the dynamic mirror in 5X00, 6X00, 7X00 series) compensates for very small \nand fast changes in the press speed and angular position.\n● The dynamic prism (or mirror) is an optical device which moves lasers with or against the PIP drum \nrotation direction.\n● The dynamic prism receives signals from the press encoder indicating the current angular position \nof the drums every 2 ms. This enables the motor controller to compensate for press rotation \ninconsistency by changing the rotation speed as required.\n● All events and processes in the press affect the main motor speed by adding of removing a load to \nand from the system.\n2 Chapter 2  Theory — DP POS — Dynamic mirror'), Document(metadata={'ratingResponse': {'number_of_votes': 0, 'rating': 0.0}, 'persona': 'Engineer', 'format': 'pdf', 'description': 'This document provides an overview of the theory of the dynamic POS and the dynamic mirror as well asexamples of the types of problems encountered when running the diagnostic tools for the dynamic POS andthe dynamic mirror. CA293-07770. 2 Theory — DP POS — Dynamic mirror\n● An image is created on the PI P drum by the writing head.\n● The created separation is transfer red to the blanket cylinder (ITM).\n● From the blanket cylinder, the separati on is transferred to the substrate.\n● After the image is completed, the substrate moves out through the tran sport system to the stacker/exit\nunit.\n● All events and processes in the press affect the main motor speed by adding of removing a load to and\nfrom the system.\n● The press speed is controlled by the Baldor/Servostar control ler driver, but the reaction time of the\ncontroller is relatively slow  when compensating for speed.\n● The dynamic prism (or the dynamic mirror in 5X00,  6X00, 7X00 series) compensates for very small and\nfast changes in the press speed and angular position.\n● The dynamic prism (or mirror) is an optical device  which moves lasers with  or against the PIP drum\nrotation direction.\n● The dynamic prism receives signals from the press en coder indicating the current angular position of\nthe drums every 2 ms. This enables the motor controller to compensate for press rotation inconsistency\nby changing the rotation speed as required.\n● All events and processes in the press affect the main motor speed by adding of removing a load to and\nfrom the system.Dynamic POS and Dynamic Mirror Technical Service\n2 Chapter 2   Theory — DP POS — Dynamic mirror CA293–07770 Rev 02')]

User Input:  DLC unit
Ground Truth: ### Replacing the Screw on the DLC Shaft\n\n#### Overview\nThis document describes how to fix the DLC shaft in the duplex unit. The procedure involves replacing the screw on the DLC shaft to ensure proper functioning and prevent breakage.\n\n#### Prerequisites\n- None\n\n#### Estimated Installation Time\n- 15 minutes\n\n#### Special Skills\n- None\n\n#### Special Jigs and Tools\n- None\n\n#### Kit Part Number\n- CA001-06990 – DLC clamp – machined screw kit\n\n#### Kit Contents\n- CA001-06840: Machine screw (Qty: 1)\n- CA001-06850: Spacer (Qty: 1)\n\n#### Steps to Replace the Screw on the DLC Shaft\n1. **Shut down the press power.**\n2. **Open the lower entrance doors of the engine and lower the duplex unit.**\n3. **Slide the DLC shaft towards the entrance of the engine.**\n\nFor detailed instructions, refer to the document [Replacing the Screw on the DLC Shaft](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241466) (TS5EM-00006, HP Indigo Ltd., Page 3-4).\n\n### Testing the DLC Motor Activation\n1. **From Print Care, open the Duplex diagnostics screen.**\n2. **Check the DLC motor activation and verify the position sensors indication accordingly.**\n   - On the user interface, tap **Motor – Up**. Visually ensure that the DLC reaches the front position.\n   - On the user interface, tap **Motor – Down**. Visually ensure that the DLC reaches the rear position.\n   - On the user interface, tap **Motor – Middle**. Visually ensure that the DLC reaches the middle position.\n\nFor detailed instructions, refer to the document [Replacing MR1 Duplex Unit with 12000 Duplex Unit](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/38559) (CA493-05910, HP Indigo Ltd., Page 96).\n\n### Testing the Duplex Pressure and Valves\n1. **Switch the Vacuum/Pressure switch to Pressure.**\n2. **Open Valve 1.**\n   - CAUTION: When you lay the paper on the DLC, keep your hands away from the DLC because it may move as the press is in Standby.\n3. **Lay down the paper. Make sure there is air blowing in the DLC in valves 3-8, but not in valves 1, 2, 9, and 10.**\n4. **Shut off Valve 1.**\n5. **Open Valve 2.**\n6. **Lay down the paper. Make sure there is suction in the DLC in valves 2, 9, but not in valves 3-8 and 10.**\n7. **Shut off Valve 2.**\n8. **Open Valve 3.**\n9. **Lay down the paper. Make sure there is suction in the DLC in valves 1, 10, but not in valves 2-9.**\n\nFor detailed instructions, refer to the document [Replacing MR1 Duplex Unit with 12000 Duplex Unit](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/38559) (CA493-05910, HP Indigo Ltd., Page 100).\n\n### Sources\n1. [Replacing the Screw on the DLC Shaft](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241466) (TS5EM-00006, HP Indigo Ltd., Page 3-4)\n2. [Replacing MR1 Duplex Unit with 12000 Duplex Unit](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/38559) (CA493-05910, HP Indigo Ltd., Page 96, 100)

User Input:  jump over seam calibration
Ground Truth: ### Calibrating the Jump-over-seam (JOS)\n\n#### Procedure for HP Indigo 6000 Digital Press\n\n1. **Ensure Software Version**: Make sure that press software version 16.3 is installed.\n2. **Check BID Stations**: Perform the steps in checking the BID stations.\n3. **Clear Saved Values**:\n   - Navigate to `bidEngageTopic > bidEngageHwType`. Clear the Saved value.\n   - Navigate to `bidEngageTopic->forceEngageProfile`. Clear the Saved value.\n   - Navigate to `bidEngageTopic->bypassJumpOverSeam`. Clear the Saved value.\n4. **Turn Off Press Software**: Turn off the press software.\n5. **Run System Initialization**: Run `systabinit` from `C:\\unicorn\\Release\\systab_setup.bat`.\n6. **Restart Press Software**: Start the press software.\n\n[Reference](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9858620-9858687-16)\n\n#### Software Version 3.1 New Features and Improvements\n\n- **BID Engage Calibration**: The BID engage jump over seam calibration is now performed using the ILS.\n- **Menu Navigation**: \n  - Go to `Menu > Ink and BIDs > BID Engage`\n  - Select `BID Jos With ILS`\n\n[Reference](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/34769)\n\n#### HP Indigo WS6800 Digital Press Jump Over Seam Enrichment Webinar\n\n- **Webinar Details**: This webinar includes Jump Over Seam Enrichment for the HP Indigo WS6800 Digital Press.\n- **Duration**: 0.50 hour(s)\n\n[Reference](https://hp-gsb.docebosaas.com/learn/course/424)\n\n#### Print Quality Troubleshooting\n\n1. **Check Jump Over Seam Components**:\n   - Check that cams are OK.\n   - Ensure cams are fully connected to the motor axle.\n   - Verify that the flag is connected properly.\n\n[Reference](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9237545_en-US-6)\n\n### Sources List\n1. **Calibrating the Jump-over-seam (JOS)**: [Document](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9858620-9858687-16), Page 1.\n2. **Software version 3.1 New features and improvements**: [Document](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/34769), Page 37.\n3. **HP Indigo WS6800 Digital Press Jump Over Seam Enrichment webinar**: [Webinar](https://hp-gsb.docebosaas.com/learn/course/424).\n4. **Print Quality Troubleshooting**: [Document](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9237545_en-US-6), Page 30.

User Input:  SETTING PARS
Ground Truth: To set up the PARS (Print Area Registration System) for HP Indigo presses, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Connections at the Air Pressure Manifold**:\n   - For press S/N 50110369 and below, and for HP Indigo 20000 Digital Press, locate the vacuum generator at the bottom of the EC (Electrical Cabinet).\n   - For press S/N 50110370 and above, locate the vacuum generator at the PARS manifold.\n   - Ensure there are no sharp bends in the vacuum hose all the way to the manifold.\n   - Verify that the quick fittings in the generator and the manifold are closed tightly ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/34757), page 43).\n\n2. **Main Air Pressure Setting**:\n   - Verify that the press main air pressure setting is 6 Bar.\n   - If the setting is correct, proceed with the following procedures:\n     - Open the rear door of the engine.\n     - Go back to the diagnostic screen and activate the vacuum.\n     - Use the PIP foil strip you cut earlier to block the suction cups ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/34757), page 43).\n\n3. **Low Vacuum Level Troubleshooting**:\n   - If the vacuum level is under 700 mBar, perform the following steps:\n     - Check the D-type air tube connection to ensure they are completely seated and not leaking.\n     - Tighten the adjustment screws if there are leaks.\n     - Verify that the vacuum quick fitting is not leaking.\n     - Activate the vacuum in the main menu of the press computer via: Diagnostics > PARS.\n     - Refer to the Vacuum level gauge; the minimum level should be 700 mBar.\n     - If there is no vacuum or if the level is below 700 mBar, check the vacuum pump.\n     - Ensure the knob on the pump is turned clockwise as far as it will go.\n     - Verify that the air tubes are connected properly to the vacuum pump.\n     - If there are no leaks and the required vacuum level is not achieved, consider replacing the pump ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_8428544-7934713-16), page 1).\n\n### Sources:\n1. PARS Service, HP Indigo, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/34757), page 43.\n2. Low vacuum level — Troubleshooting, HP Indigo, [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_8428544-7934713-16), page 1.

User Input:  CA493-05520
Ground Truth: The document titled \'Fuji Driver Installation\'' (catalog number CA493-05520) provides detailed instructions on how to install the Fuji driver in the ink cabinet for various HP Indigo Digital Press models. Here are some key steps from the document:\n\n1. **Preparation**:\n   - From the kit, take the metal bracket adapter [CA446-41470] and connect it to the Fuji driver so that the driver can be attached to the rail in the ink cabinet.\n   - Install the Fuji driver onto the rail. Put the top side over the rail and push the bottom side until it clicks ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/37999), page 12).\n\n2. **Installation**:\n   - Remove the cable bracket cover at the bottom of the driver.\n   - Slide open the cover of the driver to access the wiring ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/37999), page 6).\n\n3. **Connection**:\n   - Remove the 2 screws on the SAS cage bracket and pull the cage out slightly. Be careful not to damage the wires and tubes connected to the cage.\n   - Use a flat screwdriver to disconnect the SAS.P_IDU D-type connector.\n   - Use a 5mm socket to remove the screws from the base of the D-type connector ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/37999), page 9).\n\n4. **Reconnection**:\n   - Reconnect the D-type connector that was removed above ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/37999), page 15).\n\n5. **Validation**:\n   - To test the installation, go to: Menu > Press Service Center > Diagnostics and Troubleshooting > Diagnostics.\n   - Open the relevant ink station tab ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/37999), page 18).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Fuji Driver Installation, CA493-05520, HP Indigo, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/37999), pages 6, 9, 12, 15, 18.

User Input:  A demonstration on how to properly calibrate density for my inks.
Ground Truth: To properly calibrate the density for your inks, follow these steps:\n\n### Calibrating HP ElectroInk White Plus\n\n1. **Substrate Definitions**:\n   - In the General tab, set FaceStock to Transparent.\n   - In the Color Control tab, set Gloss level to Semi matte.\n   - Set the optical density of the substrate as measured manually using a calibrated X-Rite densitometer (in G-mode).\n   - When calibrating transparent substrates, place a white sheet beneath the substrate.\n\n2. **Calibrating HP ElectroInk White Plus**:\n   - Install a transparent substrate (not a label substrate) in the press.\n   - Define the clear substrate as described in step 1.\n   - Perform a full color calibration.\n   - Once the calibration has successfully completed, print a separate solid white patch.\n   - Place a solid, glossy black sheet with an OD of 1.75 or more under the white printed patch, and check the optical density of the white patch using an external densitometer set to the cyan channel.\n   - The desired optical density is 0.32 with a tolerance of +/- 0.01. If the optical density is 0.32, the White Plus color is properly calibrated.\n   - If the optical density is not 0.32, open the color calibration wizard.\n   - In the Calibration type area, select Full-High accuracy.\n   - In the How to run area, select Step by step - high flexibility.\n   - Click Next.\n   - Select the type of screen you want to calibrate.\n   - Click Next.\n   - Verify that White ink is selected.\n   - Click Next.\n   - Select Standard method, and click Optical Density.\n   - Adjust the White ink optical density as needed:\n     - If the optical density is more than 0.32, decrease the White ink optical density.\n     - If the optical density is less than 0.32, increase the White ink optical density.\n   - Finish the calibration and check the optical density again.\n   - Repeat the calibration steps if necessary until the optical density is 0.32 with a tolerance of +/- 0.01.\n\n3. **Working with Non-Transparent Substrates**:\n   - When working with HP ElectroInk White Plus ink on any substrate that is not clear or transparent, select the Inherit color calibration check box, and in the Scroll tab, select the clear or transparent substrate that was used for the HP ElectroInk White Plus color calibration.\n\nFor more detailed instructions, you can refer to the following sources:\n- [Performing color calibration with HP ElectroInk White Plus](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9604904-9604549-16)\n- [Calibrating ink density](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9822715-9508168-16)\n\n### Sources:\n1. Performing color calibration with HP ElectroInk White Plus, page 1, [link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9604904-9604549-16)\n2. Calibrating ink density, page 1, [link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9822715-9508168-16)

User Input:  the white paper\nHP Indigo for Food Packaging Printing Regulatory Overview (4AA4-8153ENW, February 2015).
Ground Truth: The white paper \'HP Indigo for Food Packaging Printing Regulatory Overview (4AA4-8153ENW, February 2015)\' provides detailed information on the regulatory status of HP Indigo ElectroInk for food packaging applications. This document outlines the compliance of HP Indigo ElectroInk with key worldwide regulations for food contact materials and specifies well-defined conditions of use. \n\n### Key Points from the White Paper:\n\n1. **Regulatory Compliance**:\n   - The white paper details the status of HP Indigo ElectroInk under various global regulations for food contact materials.\n   - It emphasizes that HP Indigo ElectroInk is not intended for direct food contact but can be used in specific applications under defined conditions.\n\n2. **Risk Assessment**:\n   - Customers are encouraged to perform their own risk assessments for their specific applications.\n   - HP Indigo provides information to assist customers and their laboratories in conducting proper risk assessments.\n\n3. **In-Mold Labeling (IML)**:\n   - Although IML is not specifically referred to in the white paper, HP Indigo ElectroInk can be used in IML applications with appropriate risk assessments.\n   - IML applications typically involve surface printing and overcoating with an overprint varnish to protect the printed label and ensure compliance with food contact regulations.\n\n4. **Migration and Set-Off Risks**:\n   - The document highlights potential risks such as migration from the printed surface through the label and container, set-off inside winded rolls, and set-off inside stacked labels or containers.\n   - Customers are advised to consider these risks and ensure that the varnish used is approved for direct or indirect food contact and low migration.\n\n5. **Responsibility and Compliance**:\n   - HP Indigo is not responsible for materials and processes beyond its control.\n   - Customers must ensure their products comply with regulatory requirements and perform their own risk assessments.\n\nFor more detailed information, you can refer to the white paper directly or contact HP customer care for access to the document.\n\n### Sources:\n1. User Input:  how to raise it
Ground Truth: To raise the HP Indigo 6K Digital Press, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Leveling the Engine**:\n   - When leveling the process direction of the engine:\n     - If you raise corner B with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt, ensure that you also raise corner A with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt.\n     - Similarly, if you raise corner D with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt, ensure that you also raise corner C with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt.\n   - When leveling the perpendicular direction of the engine:\n     - If you raise corner B with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt, ensure that you also raise corner D with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt.\n     - Similarly, if you raise corner A with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt, ensure that you also raise corner C with two rotations of the pad adjustment bolt.\n   - Repeat this process until the readings are the same. Note that the calibration can be successful even if the bubble is not 100% in the middle of the window ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/52556), page 30).\n\n2. **Raising the Top of the Jig**:\n   - Loosen the flag screws and move the flag down. Remove the flag.\n   - Move the homing sensor up.\n   - Raise the top of the jig.\n   - Raise the nuts and lower the top of the jig onto the actuator.\n   - Install the gas spring jig on the gas spring ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/13496), page 108).\n\n3. **Installing C-Clips**:\n   - Install the top C-clip.\n   - Install the bottom C-clip, ensuring that it sits in its slot. Push the gas spring against the actuator to ensure proper placement.\n   - Raise the nuts and the top of the gas spring jig.\n   - Remove the tie-wrap from the gas spring jig ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/13496), page 116).\n\n### Sources:\n1. HP Indigo 6K Digital Press Installation, page 30, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/52556)\n2. ILP Service - 30000, page 108, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/13496)\n3. ILP Service - 30000, page 116, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/13496)

User Input:  HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign CC2024
Ground Truth: ### HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign CC2024\n\n#### Overview\nHP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign version 19.1 is the latest release designed to work with Adobe InDesign CC2024. This version addresses several issues reported in previous versions and includes various improvements and new features.\n\n#### Installation Steps\nTo install HP SmartStream Designer 19.1 for Adobe InDesign CC2024, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Ensure Adobe InDesign is Closed**: Before starting the installation, make sure that Adobe InDesign is not running.\n2. **Run the Installer**: Double-click the installer file for either Mac or PC. The installer window will open.\n3. **Follow On-Screen Instructions**: Proceed with the on-screen instructions to complete the installation.\n4. **Open Adobe InDesign**: Once the installation is complete, open Adobe InDesign. The SmartStream Designer menu and workspace will be added to the application.\n5. **Verify Installation**: From the Adobe InDesign menu, select `Window > SmartStream Designer > About` to verify that version 19.1 is installed.\n\n#### System Requirements\n- **Adobe Illustrator CC2024 (64-Bit)**\n- **RAM**: 16 GB\n- **Operating System**:\n  - **Mac**: MacOS 13 (Ventura) or MacOS 14 (Sonoma)\n  - **PC**: Windows 10 or Windows 11\n\n#### Important Notes\n- **Java and Barcode Studio**: Separate installations of Java and Barcode Studio are required. The installer will check for the required Java version and prompt you to install it if necessary. For Barcode Studio, version 16.6.3 is required, and it can be installed during or after the SmartStream Designer installation.\n- **POSIX Path Compatibility**: For Mac users, Adobe InDesign version 19.4 or later uses POSIX paths, which are not compatible with HP SmartStream Designer. Users should disable POSIX paths to ensure compatibility.\n\n#### Additional Resources\n- **HP SmartStream Designer Quick Links**: Provides quick access to all documentation needs, including user guides and how-to guides for various features like HP Mosaic and HP Collage.\n- **HP PrintOS Marketplace**: For purchasing licenses and accessing additional resources.\n\nFor more detailed information, you can refer to the [HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign v19.1 CC2024 - Release Notes](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049).\n\n### Sources\n1. [HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign v19.1 CC2024 - Release Notes](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049) - Page 1, 3, 4, 6\n2. [HP SmartStream Designer Quick Links](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/43808) - Page 3

Ground Truth: ### HP SmartStream Designer 19.1 for Adobe InDesign CC2024\n\n#### Overview\nHP SmartStream Designer for InDesign version 19.1 is a new version for Adobe InDesign CC2024. This version addresses issues reported in previous versions and includes several enhancements and new features.\n\n#### Key Features and Enhancements\n1. **Designer Workspace Setup**:\n   - In the Adobe InDesign Workspaces list, select `Designer Tools > Basic` or `Designer Tools > Advanced Workspace`. The SmartStream Designer panels will open.\n   - Alternatively, manually open the SmartStream Designer panels from the `Window` menu by selecting `SmartStream Designer` and then the specific panels ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=10).\n\n2. **License Code Registration**:\n   - From the Adobe InDesign menu, select `Window > SmartStream Designer > About`.\n   - In the About window, click `Register`, enter the registration code received, and click `OK`.\n   - Click `OK` to close the About window ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=10).\n\n3. **Trial and Functionality**:\n   - The licensed edition provides full functionality. A 30-day trial with full functionality is available for first-time installations.\n   - Post-trial, without a license code, the following limitations apply:\n     - Create PDF output is disabled.\n     - Create HPD is limited to direct creation to HP PrintOS Composer only ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=10).\n\n4. **Connecting to HP SmartStream Composer**:\n   - From the SmartStream Designer menu, select `Preferences`.\n   - Click the `New` button next to the Press Name, enter the Composer name or IP Address, then click `OK`.\n   - Click `OK` to close the Preferences window ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=10).\n\n#### Known Issues and Workarounds\n1. **Facing Pages**:\n   - For documents with facing pages and a channel placed on both, imposition results may be incorrect. Place an image channel on every page instead ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=13).\n   - For facing pages jobs with elements placed on one entire page, imposition preview and output may be incorrect under certain conditions. Turning \'Facing Pages\' off can resolve this ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=13).\n\n2. **Imposition**:\n   - N_up imposition does not support distribute records. Use 1_up with Step and Repeat if applicable ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=13).\n\n3. **Multiple Layouts**:\n   - Distribution is not supported for jobs with multiple impositions that have multiple size pages imposed on separate sheets with different Step and Repeat values. Create different impositions for each page size and separate output files ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=13).\n\n### Sources\n1. HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign v19.1 CC2024 - Release Notes, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=1.\n2. HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign v19.1 CC2024 - Release Notes, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=10.\n3. HP SmartStream Designer for Adobe InDesign v19.1 CC2024 - Release Notes, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/241049), page=13.

User Input:  electrometer board calibration wizard
Ground Truth: To calibrate the electrometer board using the calibration wizard, follow these detailed steps:\n\n1. **Preparation**:\n   - Ensure you have the necessary tools and jigs, specifically the CA397-06881 jig for testing the electrometer board for S3 and S4.\n   - The estimated calibration time is approximately 30 minutes ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 3).\n\n2. **Initial Setup**:\n   - Use a Digital Voltmeter (DVM) to verify that the electrometer jig foil is grounded to the press and check the appropriate box on the screen ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 7).\n   - Click the \'Next\' button at the bottom of the wizard screen and select the \'Power\' button on the next screen.\n\n3. **Voltage Verification**:\n   - Use the DVM to adjust the electrometer “0” on connector J1 of the electrometer board:\n     - Verify that the voltage between pins 1 and 3 on connector J1 is 24V and check the appropriate box on the screen ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 7).\n     - Measure the voltage between pins 2 and 4 on connector J1 and check the appropriate box on the screen ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 8).\n     - Adjust the potentiometer on the electrometer board until the voltage between pins 2 and 4 is 0.00 ± 0.01 V ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 8).\n\n4. **Reconnecting Components**:\n   - Disengage the PIP drum.\n   - Disconnect the electrometer board jig connectors from the electrometer and from the original J1 connector. Connect J1 to the electrometer ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 8).\n   - Disconnect the jig connectors from the charge roller and reconnect the original connectors.\n   - Remove the electrometer jig foil and check the appropriate box on the software screen ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 8).\n\n5. **Final Steps**:\n   - Put the press in Standby mode.\n   - Go to Main Menu > Problem Handling > CE Wizards.\n   - Select \'Electrometer Calibration\' and follow the wizard instructions, confirming each step on the screen ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), page 5).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Electrometer Calibration, CA393-09460, HP Indigo, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19637), pages 3, 5, 7, 8.

User Input:  emergency oem errors
Ground Truth: Here are some details regarding emergency OEM errors and their solutions for HP Indigo presses:\n\n1. **ILP Emergency Stop Button**:\n   - When an ILP Emergency Stop button is pressed, the following actions occur:\n     - FB nip opens\n     - FB motor is disabled\n     - Corona system stops\n     - Coating system motor stops\n     - Coating system rollers disengage\n     - Coating system pump stops\n     - Dryer system (including heater, blower, and suction) stops\n     - Buffer system tension is disabled\n   - This information is crucial for understanding the immediate effects of pressing the emergency stop button and ensuring the safety of the press and operator ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335), page 9).\n\n2. **Software Errors and Solutions**:\n   - **Error Message**: \'PLC error report: Type: UNC_FEEDBACK_ERR. Failed unit: ILP_MOTOR_CORONA_GENERATOR\'\n     - **Solution**: Reset generator power switch\n   - **High voltage error messages**:\n     - **Solution**: Check transformer oil level\n   - **ILP corona cover open**:\n     - **Solution**: Close treater\n   - **ILP corona drawer open**:\n     - **Solution**: Close corona drawer\n   - **ILP emergency line is open**:\n     - **Solution**: Close ILP doors\n   - **ILP corona air suction is too low**:\n     - **Solution**: Check for ILP corona electrode failure\n   - **Jam in corona input (Paper_detection_fault1)**:\n     - **Solution**: Remove substrate from corona input sensor\n   - **Jam in corona exit (Paper_detection_fault2)**:\n     - **Solution**: Remove substrate from corona exit sensor\n   - These solutions help in troubleshooting and resolving common software errors encountered during press operation ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9433215-9297904-16), page 1).\n\n3. **Attention Lights**:\n   - **Green light**:\n     - Always on in Printing (Proof) status\n     - Flashing in Getting Ready and Ready statuses\n   - **Yellow light**:\n     - Always on for all errors and for warning LEDs\n   - **Red light**:\n     - Flashing when the bypass key is inserted\n   - Understanding the meaning of attention lights helps in quickly identifying the status and any potential issues with the press ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4), page 29).\n\n### Sources:\n1. ILP Service and Troubleshooting, page 9, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335)\n2. Software errors, page 1, [HP Indigo](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9433215-9297904-16)\n3. The press User Guide, page 29, [HP Indigo](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4)\n\nIf you need further assistance or have more specific queries, feel free to ask!

User Input:  ink flow adjustment
Ground Truth: To adjust the ink flow on an HP Indigo press, follow these steps:\n\n### For All Press Software Versions:\n1. **In the Ink Cabinet:**\n   - Completely close all ink flow adjustment knobs for all colors (Figure 1).\n   - Use a permanent marker to mark the position of each knob.\n   - Open each knob 5¾ turns.\n\n### For Press Software Versions 5.2 and Up:\n2. **At the Computer:**\n   - From the Adjustments menu, click on \Ink Flow Calibration.\\n   - In the Ink Flow Calibration window, select one of the colors.\n   - Click \'Next.\'\n\n### Detailed Steps:\n1. **Touch Main Menu > HP Indigo Print Care.**\n2. **Select Service Level, and change the level to Customer Engineer.** The menu changes to the Customer Engineer menu.\n3. **Select Element Activation and check the following:**\n   - In the Ink tab, touch the buttons for each ink color installed.\n4. **Touch Main Menu > HP Indigo Print Care > Maintenance > Calibrations > Press Engine > Ink System.**\n5. **For every color, run the BID Ink Flow Calibration Wizard.**\n\n### References:\n- [HP Indigo service document Ink System](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24851) (Page 11)\n- [Ink Cabinet Service](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19475) (Page 104)\n- [Ink flow adjustment](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9822715-9508164-16)

User Input:  Video showing or Documentation explaining how to remove and replace this worn shaft on Exit conveyor  in Indigo 5900 Press.
Ground Truth: To remove and replace the worn shaft on the exit conveyor in the HP Indigo 5900 Press, you can follow the detailed steps provided in the HP Indigo 5900 Digital Press Installation Guide. Here is a summary of the steps:\n\n1. **Loosen the Screws**: Loosen the two screws securing the exit tray bottom switch bracket. Adjust the height so that the rubber foot touches the floor and then retighten the screws ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068), page 59).\n\n2. **Remove the Exit Tray Base**: Place the exit tray base in the exit tray compartment on the elevator. Ensure the base presence sensor reflector is in the back left corner, and the high side of the base is at the right-hand side of the compartment ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068), page 59).\n\n3. **Remove Pallet Mounts**: Remove the four pallet mounts holding the PE. At the PE front side, remove the two covers that are over the forklift holes in the PE chassis ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068), page 11).\n\n4. **Lift the PE**: Have a qualified forklift operator gently and carefully lift the PE from the pallet. Place a piece of packing foam or padding between the PE and the forklift to prevent scratches or other damage ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068), page 11).\n\n5. **Roll the PE**: Roll the PE to its position in the press room. Orient it properly as defined by the site preparation and obtain customer approval for the final position of the PE. Reinstall the forklift hole covers ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068), page 11).\n\n### Sources:\n1. HP Indigo 5900 Digital Press Installation Guide, page 59, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068)\n2. HP Indigo 5900 Digital Press Installation Guide, page 11, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068)\n\nFor a more detailed explanation and visual guidance, you can refer to the [HP Indigo 5900 Digital Press Installation Guide](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/30068).

User Input:  BID
Ground Truth: ### Binary Ink Developer (BID) Overview\n\nThe Binary Ink Developer (BID) is a crucial component in the HP Indigo digital press, playing a significant role in the image generation process. Here are some key points about BID:\n\n1. **Functionality**: The press uses BID to build ink inside the BID unit and transfer it to the image areas on the Photo Imaging Plate (PIP). Excess ink flows back into the BID and out to the ink tank. Each BID unit is responsible for generating a different color separation, although the units are identical ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4), page 217).\n\n2. **Components**:\n   - **BID Base**: The base part of the BID unit.\n   - **Developer Roller**: Works in conjunction with the BID base to develop the ink.\n\n3. **Configurations**:\n   - **Single-unit BID**: The BID unit, comprising the BID base and the developer roller, can only be replaced as a whole.\n   - **BID-P**: The BID unit comprises two components—the BID base and the developer roller—which can be replaced separately ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4), page 217).\n\n### Installing the BID Base and BID Handle\n\nTo install the BID base and BID handle, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Components Required**:\n   - BID Base (C8Q07C) for BIDs 1–7.\n   - BID Developer (C8Q01B) for BIDs 1–7.\n   - BID Handle (CA445-51093) for BIDs 1–6.\n\n2. **Installation Steps**:\n   - Insert the BID Base into the BID Drawer.\n   - Insert the BID Developer into the BID Base and lock it in place with clamps.\n   - Install the BID Handle onto the outer front side of the BID Base using a 5mm key to tighten 4 M6 screws.\n   - Spray Imaging Oil onto BID Developer and BID Base tubes ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9862126-9713016-16), page 1).\n\n### BID Engage System Service\n\nThe BID engage system service involves several procedures:\n\n1. **Inspection**:\n   - BID engage cable and sensor connection.\n   - Front and rear BID engage motor connectors and cables.\n\n2. **Cleaning**:\n   - BID sensors.\n   - Front and rear BID sensors.\n\n3. **Replacement**:\n   - BDU (BID Drive Unit).\n   - BID sensors.\n   - BID engage motor.\n   - BID Motor (MOP) and its housing ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9373161_en-US-6), page 3).\n\n### Sources List\n\n1. **Installing the BID Base and BID Handle**:\n   - Document: Installing the BID Base and BID Handle\n   - Author: UDP\n   - Link: [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9862126-9713016-16)\n   - Page: 1\n\n2. **BID Engage System**:\n   - Document: BID Engage System\n   - Author: UDP\n   - Link: [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9373161_en-US-6)\n   - Page: 3\n\n3. **Binary Ink Developer (BID)**:\n   - Document: the press User Guide\n   - Author: UDP\n   - Link: [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4)\n   - Page: 217

User Input:  AUTO BIAS
Ground Truth: ### Troubleshooting Auto Bias Failure on HP Indigo WS6600 Digital Press\n\nIf you encounter an Auto Bias failure on the HP Indigo WS6600 Digital Press, follow these steps to resolve the issue:\n\n1. **Access the Required Directory:**\n   - From the Desktop, select \'My Computer.\'\n   - Navigate to the directory: `C:\\UNICORN\\RELEASE`.\n\n2. **Run the ISTOREFORMAT.BAT File:**\n   - Locate and run the `ISTOREFORMAT.BAT` file in the directory.\n\n3. **Restart the PC:**\n   - Perform two consecutive restarts of the PC.\n\n4. **Install a Linearity Patch (if applicable):**\n   - Follow the general instructions provided for installing a linearity patch if required.\n\n5. **Charge Roller Leveling:**\n   - Run the charge roller leveling process:\n     - Go to `Print Care > Diagnostic and Troubleshooting > Tests (second tab) > Engine > Charge Roller > Leveling Calibration`.\n   - Run the Auto Bias wizard.\n   - If necessary, bypass the charge roller activation:\n     - In Systab, set `BypassTableTopic > crJosActive` to `True`.\n   - Run the Auto Bias wizard again.\n\n### References:\n- [Operator Troubleshooting Guide for the HP Indigo WS6600 Digital Press](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9547131_en-US-4) (Page 24)\n- [Auto Bias Fails - HP Indigo WS6600 Digital Press](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9604904-9604516-16) (Page 1)\n- [Charge Roller Service Document](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/35279) (Page 23)\n\n### Sources List:\n1. User Input:  v electrode
Ground Truth: The V-electrode calibration is a process used in HP Indigo digital presses to ensure accurate color calibration. Here are some key points about V-electrode calibration:\n\n1. **Automatic Calibration**: The V-electrode calibration automatically runs during a cold start. It is recommended to use the V-electrode calibration when installing a new ink or a new BID (Binary Ink Developer). Default parameters can be used for troubleshooting, such as color calibration failures ([source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4), page 99).\n\n2. **Manual Calibration**: The V-electrode was previously calibrated during every automatic or manual color calibration. To reduce the amount of printed pages and time, the frequency of V-electrode calibration during automatic color calibration has been reduced to every three color calibrations. This can be configured in the Advanced Color Calibration settings ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/31989), page 5).\n\n3. **Configuration**: You can configure the option of calibrating the V-electrode during Advanced Color Calibration to save time and printed pages. This can be done by navigating to Menu > Print Quality > Advanced Calibration, and under the Options tab, selecting or clearing the V-electrode option for the relevant substrates ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33563), page 13).\n\n### Sources:\n1. the press User Guide, page 99, [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_7606095_en-US-4)\n2. HP Indigo 12000 Digital Press - Operator Quick Guide, page 5, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/31989)\n3. Software Ver 3.1 Operator Quick Guide, page 13, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/33563)

User Input:  How to guide with steps including screenshots on how to connect a new press to PrintOS
Ground Truth: To connect a new press to PrintOS, follow these detailed steps:\n\n### Step 1: Check for Updates\n1. **Select Check for updates**: Ensure your press software is up to date.\n2. **Install I-Serve**: In the Solution tab, click Install to install the I-Serve.\n3. **Follow the Wizard**: Follow the instructions in the installation wizard.\n4. **Start the Press Software**: Once the installation is complete, start the press software.\n\n### Step 2: Validate the I-Serve Connection\n1. **Connect to I-Serve**: Right-click on the I-Serve icon and select Connect.\n2. **Log Viewer**: Right-click on the I-Serve icon and select Log Viewer.\n3. **Verify Transfer**: Verify that the transfer was successful in the HP IndigoServe Log Viewer.\n\n### Step 3: Check the PrintOS Connection and TLS 1.2\n1. **Internet Connection**: Open [HP Website](https://www.hp.com/) to check the internet connection. If this fails, refer to the HP PrintOS Production Pro Network Requirements Guide.\n2. **PrintOS Connection**: Go to `C:\\IndigoAccess` and run the Indigo Access Tool. If this fails, refer to the HP PrintOS Production Pro Network Requirements Guide.\n3. **PrintOS URL**: Select Print Preference > HP PrintOS Preferences > HP PrintOS.\n   - **China**: [PrintOS China](https://www.printos.cn)\n   - **Rest of the World**: [PrintOS](https://www.printos.com)\n4. **Enable TLS 1.2 (Windows 7 Only)**:\n   - Select Start > Run. Type `Regedit` and click OK.\n   - Navigate to `HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\\SYSTEM\\CurrentControlSet\\Control\\SecurityProviders\\SCHANNEL\\Protocols\\TLS 1.2`.\n   - If TLS 1.2 is missing, install `TLS1.2_Enable_SysHotFix_1.0.1`.\n\n### Step 4: Provision/Connect the DFE on PrintOS Account\n1. **Credentials**: Use the credentials provided by the customer. If credentials are not available, refer the customer to the Production Pro User Guide for steps to configure PrintOS.\n2. **Resource Manager**: Review Resource Manager with the customer.\n\n### Step 5: Demonstrate and Provide Training\n1. **Walk-Thrus**: Demonstrate to the customer how to access and use Walk-Thrus.\n2. **E-Learning Modules**: Provide the customer with links to relevant E-Learning modules.\n3. **Training Program**: Explain the blended training program, including E-Learning and Training Center options for operator certification.\n4. **Operator Certification**: Encourage the customer to certify their operators to ensure they are up to date with the latest capabilities and certified for operational efficiency.\n\n### Screenshots\nUnfortunately, I cannot provide screenshots directly, but you can refer to the detailed steps and the provided links for visual guidance.\n\n### References\n1. [Press Software Installation 16.3](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9858200_en-US-6) - Page 18\n2. [Windows Server 2019 Installation Gen10 Prod Pro Commercial](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47262) - Page 49\n\n### Sources List\n1. Press Software Installation 16.3, Page 18, HP Indigo, [Link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_9858200_en-US-6)\n2. Windows Server 2019 Installation Gen10 Prod Pro Commercial, Page 49, HP Indigo, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/47262)
