User Input:  A statement regarding HP ElectroInk compliance to EC regulation 1223/2009
Ground Truth: HP ElectroInk complies with various regulatory requirements, including the EC regulation 1223/2009. Here are some key points regarding its compliance:\n\n1. **Chemical Inventory Status**: All chemical substances in HP ElectroInk products have been notified or are exempt from notification under chemical substances notification laws in the EU (EINECS/ELINCS) and other countries (TDS HP Indigo ElectroInk - Technical Data Sheet - HP Indigo 5000 Series, page 2) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/36894).\n\n2. **General Regulatory Status**: HP Indigo ElectroInk does not contain substances of very high concern (SVHC) for inclusion in Annex XIV of REACH, CMRs, phthalates, bisphenols, or heavy metals. It also does not require a California Proposition 65 warning (TDS HP Indigo ElectroInk - Technical Data Sheet - HP Indigo 5000 Series, page 2) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/36894).\n\n3. **Food Packaging Regulations**: HP Indigo ElectroInk is safe and suitable for printing flexible packaging, labels, and folding cartons on the non-food contact side of the food packaging, under certain conditions of use and compliance with Good Manufacturing Practices (GMP). It meets US, European, and other regional regulatory requirements when used with specific polymeric films (TDS HP Indigo ElectroInk - Technical Data Sheet - HP Indigo 5000 Series, page 2) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/36894).\n\n4. **Swiss Ordinance Compliance**: All ingredients are on the Swiss Positive List of the Swiss Ordinance on Materials and Articles in Contact with Food (RS 817.023.21). HP Indigo ElectroInk is compliant with Nestle Guidance Note on Packaging Inks (TDS HP Indigo ElectroInk - Technical Data Sheet - HP Indigo 5000 Series, page 3) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/36894).\n\n### Sources:\n1. TDS HP Indigo ElectroInk - Technical Data Sheet - HP Indigo 5000 Series, page 2, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/36894).\n2. TDS HP Indigo ElectroInk - Technical Data Sheet - HP Indigo 5000 Series, page 3, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/36894).

User Input:  ADJUSTMENT THROUGH PAPER
Ground Truth: ### Adjusting Paper on HP Indigo Press\n\n#### Steps for Adjusting Paper on HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press\n\n1. **Open the Stacker Side Panel**:\n   - Open the stacker side panel at the rear and front.\n   - Push out the parts box through the rear exit and open the box to display the parts.\n\n2. **Install the Alignment Bracket**:\n   - Install the alignment bracket at the lower stacker-press interface using two M12 x 65 bolts and washers.\n   - Do not tighten the bolts at this stage.\n\n3. **Install the Lateral Adjustment Bracket**:\n   - Install the lateral adjustment bracket and screw using two flat Allen M8 screws.\n   - Mount the nut to the alignment bracket side of the lateral adjustment.\n\n4. **Mount Nuts to Alignment Screws**:\n   - Mount two nuts to the alignment screws as shown in the figure.\n\n5. **Bring the Stacker Close to the Press**:\n   - Bring the stacker close to the press.\n\n6. **Insert Securing Pads**:\n   - Insert the securing pads under the stacker feet while the stacker is still on the wheels, and before lowering it to the floor.\n   - Insert a foot pad under the stacker foot and two cut sheets of slick paper on top of the pads. The slick paper will allow the stacker to be moved to its final position.\n   - Repeat for the other stacker feet.\n\n[Reference: Installation - HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press, CA393-09964, Page 64](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918)\n\n#### Steps for Adjusting Paper Exit Belt Tension on HP Indigo Press\n\n1. **Press the Emergency Stop Button**:\n   - Ensure safety by pressing the emergency stop button.\n\n2. **Loosen Set Screws**:\n   - Loosen the set screws to remove pulleys and belt.\n\n3. **Loosen Screws to Adjust Belt Tension**:\n   - Loosen the screws to adjust belt tension.\n\n4. **Take Tension Measurement**:\n   - Bring the paper exit feed box out of the press, but do not remove it completely.\n   - Remove the plastic cover.\n   - Take a tension measurement of the paper exit belt by holding the meter so that its microphone is one cm above the mid-point of the upper belt section.\n   - Pluck the belt close to the microphone as one would a guitar string. The reading in Hz appears in the meter window.\n   - Pull the belt by hand until a different section of the belt is at the measurement point and take a second measurement.\n   - Repeat the process to take a third measurement.\n   - Take an average of the three readings.\n\n5. **Adjust Belt Tension**:\n   - If the average of the three readings is not 140 ± 10 Hz, adjust the belt tension by loosening the four screws securing the motor, moving the motor to loosen or tighten the belt as necessary, and then tightening the screws.\n   - Repeat the measurement steps until the desired tension is achieved.\n\n6. **Reinstall Components**:\n   - Reinstall the plastic cover and the paper exit feed box.\n\n[Reference: HP Indigo Service Document Belt Tension Adjustment, MNU-1667-41, Page 15-16](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24983)\n\n### Sources\n1. Installation - HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press, CA393-09964, Page 64, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29918)\n2. HP Indigo Service Document Belt Tension Adjustment, MNU-1667-41, Page 15-16, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24983)

The resistance for the paper transport in the turning unit is extremely low\n   thanks to the air-cushioned 90º turning unit.\n• TU-A (Turn Unit Air)\n– The current of air is generated by the side channel blower in the fan   supplying the turning unit and provides a cushion of air around the 90º   turning bar in the turning unit through a flexible hose system.\n• UP (Underpass)\n– The paper web undercrossing is not provided with its own drive for    transporting the paper web. The paper web is drawn through the paper\n   web undercrossing by the post-processing module.\n0.6.3  Special technical features\n• TU (Turn Unit)\n– shortest setting-up time– simple operation– paper web is completely protected– small friction forces by air-washed around rollers– enlarged roll diameters  (less curl, transport of thick paper possible)• TU-A (Turn Unit Air)\n– independent air supply system– no facility installation nor other air source needed\n• UP (Underpass)\n– can be walked on– paper web is completely protected\n0.6.4  Basic equipment\n• TU (Turn Unit)\n– Deflector roller raised– Deflector roller lowered– Turning bar with adjustment unit– Turning bar fixed\n• TU-A (Turn Unit Air)\n– Turning bar with air\n• UP (Underpass)\n– Paper web undercrossing UP 500 - 750\n0.6.5  Technical versions\n– none\n0.6.6  Optional equipment\n– none\nOverview'), Document(metadata={'ratingResponse': {'number_of_votes': 0, 'rating': 0.0}, 'persona': 'Engineer', 'format': 'pdf', 'description': 'This document applies to the following products: HP Indigo press 5000. User Input:  information about how to use technical inks in the L&P DFE
Ground Truth: To use technical inks in the L&P DFE (Digital Front End), follow these steps:\n\n1. **Objective**: Understand that HP Production Pro L&P is the default DFE for all L&P presses. It was not designed to support commercial presses. This configuration is triggered by customers with a need to manage spot colors for L&P applications (mainly light folding-carton, glue-applied labels, and tags).\n\n2. **Part Numbers**:\n   - For new sales of Commercial press with Production Pro for Indigo L&P:\n     - HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press: H0H80B - P. Pro for L&P IN100T WS SYS Z8G4 TOWER\n     - HP Indigo 12000/HD: H0H82B - P. Pro for L&P IN150T SYS Z8G4 TOWER\n   - Converting Production Pro to Production Pro for Indigo L&P:\n     - IN100 HP Indigo 7900 Digital Press: H0H95A - P. Pro for L&P V7.X IN100 SW only (Virtual)\n     - IN150 HP Indigo 12000/HD Digital Press: Z0C17A - P. Pro for L&P V7.X IN150T SW only (Virtual)\n\n3. **Licensing**:\n   - For new sales, the license is provided by a sales admin triggered by the DFE P/N appearing in the sales order (same process as Production Pro L&P).\n   - For conversions to Production Pro L&P v7.x from HP SmartStream Production Pro 6.x, generate a new license using the Global Graphics license tool.\n\n4. **L&P Workflow Limitations**:\n   - **Imposition**: In the L&P Prepress, the main use of imposition is for stepping the jobs on the sheet or ganging a number of jobs on different lanes. Commercial impositions (saddle stitch, perfect bound, etc.) are not built-in templates. To use such impositions, create them externally in the Composer/Designer plug-in of InDesign or in another external imposition software.\n\nFor more detailed information, you can refer to the [Limitations of Prod Pro L&P for Commercial presses](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/42981) document.\n\n### Sources:\n- Limitations of Prod Pro L&P for Commercial presses, TN-2284, HP Indigo, [Link](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/42981), Page 2.

User Input:  drawer 2 keeps on skewing
Ground Truth: To address the issue of drawer 2 skewing, you can follow these steps to adjust the alignment and ensure proper functioning:\n\n1. **Remove the Substrate**: Start by removing any substrate from the drawer.\n2. **Loosen the Locking Screw**: Locate and remove the locking screw of the drawer X-align mechanism. Then, loosen the drawer X-align table screw at the bottom of the drawer.\n   ![Locking screw](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/38004)\n3. **Adjust the Spikes**: Move the spikes to the drawer’s front side by rotating the spike screw head counterclockwise.\n4. **Lower the Drawer**: Bring the drawer to the lower position by rotating the belt below the drawer.\n5. **Access the Alignment Mechanism**: Open the front drawer cover to access the Spikes X-alignment mechanism while the drawer is closed.\n6. **Insert Substrate**: Turn on the power while the drawer is open. Insert 30 sheets of 750 mm substrate into the feeder drawer.\n7. **Check Distance**: Close the drawer and check the distance between the spikes and the papers (front and rear sides) by rotating the spike screw head. The distance should be 2-3 mm.\n\nFor more detailed instructions, you can refer to the [Feeder Service Document](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/38004) (Page 37).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Feeder Service Document, Page 37, HP Indigo, [Feeder Service Document](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/38004)

User Input:  Drawer 1 feeder
Ground Truth: ### Calibrating the Feeder Drawer Height\n\nTo calibrate the feeder drawer height, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Access the Top Feeder Drawer**: Lower it to the bottom.\n2. **Press the Blue Activation Button**: This will lower the drawer.\n3. **Empty the Drawer Contents**: Remove all paper from the drawer.\n4. **Close the Feeder Drawer**: The drawer will automatically rise to verify that it’s empty and then lower itself to the bottom.\n\n**Note**: If the drawer lowers itself to the bottom, continue with Step 5. If the drawer doesn’t lower, perform the following steps:\n   - Access the COM1 interface.\n   - Type: `godown 1` (where “1” is the top feeder drawer and “2” is the bottom drawer).\n   - The drawer will lower itself to the bottom.\n   - Continue with Step 5.\n\n5. **In the COM1 Interface**: Type `teachlevel<drawer number>`, e.g., `teach level 1`.\n   - “1” defines the top feeder drawer.\n   - “2” defines the bottom feeder drawer.\n6. **Verify Drawer Movement**: Ensure that the drawer lifts itself up and down and that the COM1 interface indicates (online).\n7. **Re-insert Paper**: Open the drawer, re-insert paper, and close the drawer.\n8. **Repeat Steps**: Repeat Steps 1-7 with the bottom feeder drawer.\n\n[Feeder Service TS5ES-00009](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64465) (Page 99)\n\n### Replacing the Feeder Drawer Plate\n\nTo replace the feeder drawer plate, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Remove the Feeder Drawer**: As described in the manual.\n2. **Lift the Drawer**: Place it on a working table so that the drawer plate is vertical.\n   - **Note**: 3 people are required to lift the drawer.\n\n[Feeder Service TS5ES-00009](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64465) (Page 23)\n\n### Sources\n\n1. Feeder Service TS5ES-00009, HP Indigo Ltd., [Feeder Service](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64465), Page 99.\n2. Feeder Service TS5ES-00009, HP Indigo Ltd., [Feeder Service](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/64465), Page 23.

User Input:  Ways to increase ink density
Ground Truth: To increase the ink density on HP Indigo presses, follow these steps:\n\n1. **Preparation**:\n   - Ensure you have a portable ink density meter kit (P/N EAS-1120-53) ready.\n   - Calibrate the portable ink density meter before starting the procedure.\n\n2. **At the Computer**:\n   - Set the press status to Standby.\n   - From the Diagnostics menu, click on Ink.\n   - In the Ink Properties window, go to the Density tab page and click on the ink pump button for the color you want to adjust.\n\n3. **At the Computer and Ink Cabinet**:\n   - Insert the external densitometer into the ink tank for the selected color.\n   - Aim for a reading on the external densitometer between 1.65 and 1.75.\n   - To increase the ink density, click the Add Density go button (green arrow). To decrease the ink density, add imaging oil directly into the ink tank.\n   - Stop increasing the ink density by clicking the Add Density stop button (red square) or stop adding imaging oil to decrease the ink density.\n   - Record the external densitometer reading for that color.\n\n4. **Repeat for Other Colors**:\n   - Repeat steps 3 to 6 for the remaining colors.\n\n5. **Calibration**:\n   - In the Ink Properties window, click the Calibration button.\n   - In the Density Calibration wizard, select the color you just adjusted.\n   - Do not cancel the warm-up process.\n   - Enter the value recorded in step 6 for that color in the Measured Values field.\n\nFor more detailed instructions, you can refer to the following sources:\n\n1. [HP Indigo service document Ink System](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/26603) - Page 23\n2. [HP Indigo service document Ink System](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24851) - Page 23\n3. [Calibrating ink density](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9822715-9508168-16) - Page 1\n\nSources:\n1. HP Indigo service document Ink System, Page 23, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/26603)\n2. HP Indigo service document Ink System, Page 23, [HP Indigo](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/24851)\n3. Calibrating ink density, Page 1, [HP Indigo](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9822715-9508168-16)

Ground Truth: It appears that you are interested in information related to French regulations and documentation for HP Indigo presses. Here are some relevant details:\n\n1. **Complying with the French Mineral Oil Regulation**:\n   - This document describes how to comply with the French decree of April 13, 2022. HP Indigo is phasing out HP Imaging Oil in favor of HP Imaging Oil for Packaging. Before using HP Imaging Oil for Packaging in the press, all the HP Imaging Oil must be removed from the press.\n   - The regulation applies to mineral oils containing substances that disrupt the recycling of paper or packaging waste or restrict the use of recycled materials due to the risk of these substances to human health.\n   - For detailed instructions, refer to the document TS5OM-00016 - Complying with the French Mineral Oil Regulation How-to Guide.\n   - [Source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_11568145_en-US-4) (Page 1-2)\n\n2. **Daily Maintenance Checklist for HP Indigo 10000 Digital Press**:\n   - Localized versions of this document are available in multiple languages, including French.\n   - The documentation can be accessed from HP PrintOS.\n   - [Source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_8726858_en-US-4) (Page 11)\n\n### Sources List:\n1. Complying with the French Mineral Oil Regulation, Page 1-2, [Link](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=pdf_11568145_en-US-4)\n2. Ground Truth: The document \'Ink Cabinet Service\' with catalog number CA393-04290 provides detailed instructions on how to service the ink cabinet for various HP Indigo Digital Press models. Here are some key points and revisions from the document:\n\n1. **Initial Document (Rev00)**: The initial release of the document.\n2. **Rev01**: Added HP Indigo WS6800 Digital Press to the scope and included a section on cables disconnected from the PC.\n3. **Rev02**: Expanded the scope to include several other HP Indigo Digital Press models and added sections on troubleshooting, theory of operation, and regeneration of imaging oil (RIO). Updated sections on replacing the hot water pump and purging air from the ink cabinet.\n4. **Rev03**: Updated the scope and added SIC/LIC procedures.\n5. **Rev04**: Included HP Indigo 7800 and 7900 Digital Press models.\n6. **Rev05**: Added a section on cleaning the imaging agent injection tank.\n7. **Rev06**: Introduced a new MIC board and updated the Delta Inverter parameters. Added to troubleshooting.\n8. **Rev07**: Added a section on \'Ink Tank incorrect conductivity readings\' and instructions to remove, clean (density sensor), and return the ink pump.\n\nFor more detailed information, you can refer to the document directly [here](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/19475).\n\n### Sources:\n1. Ground Truth: The HP Indigo 7K Digital Press Installation Manual provides comprehensive guidance on the installation process, including the unpacking and setup of various components. Here are some key points and steps from the manual:\n\n1. **Overview and Warranty**:\n   - Only a qualified HP Indigo Customer Engineer (CE) may open the boxes addressed to the customer. Unauthorized opening may void the warranty on the press and its parts.\n   - The manual and the corresponding installation checklist are intended for use by the CE (HP Indigo 7K Digital Press Installation, p. 1) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/48652).\n\n2. **General Information**:\n   - Upon completion of the installation, the CE must fill in and submit the online press installation and site preparation feedback reports. The CE should also fill in the Completion Of Installation (COI) form (HP Indigo 7K Digital Press Installation, p. 1) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/48652).\n\n3. **Unpacking the Press**:\n   - The HP Indigo 7K Digital Press arrives at the customer site in eight paletted boxes. Each box contains various parts, tools, and jigs. The contents list attached to Box 1 takes priority over any lists in the manual (HP Indigo 7K Digital Press Installation, p. 9) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/48652).\n\n4. **Installation Team and Schedule**:\n   - The installation should be conducted over 3 days using a team consisting of a CE and an electrician. Several parts of the installation must be performed concurrently (Installation overview, p. 1) [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9578977-9578004-16).\n\n5. **Day 1 Activities**:\n   - Verifying the site preparation, unpacking the press, and installing and leveling the press engine, feeder, and stacker. The DFE installation should also be performed on Day 1 (Day 1 Activities – Press Delivery and Leveling – 8 hours, p. 1) [source](https://kcs-dev.corp.hpicloud.net/api/v1/extras_kaas/render_url?documentID=ish_9578977-9578014-16).\n\n6. **Detailed Steps for Unpacking and Installing Components**:\n   - The manual provides detailed steps for unpacking and installing various components such as the printing engine, feeder, ink cabinet, utility cabinet, and stacker. Each step includes specific instructions and illustrations to ensure proper setup (HP Indigo 7K Digital Press Installation, p. 71) [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/48652).\n\n### Sources List:\n1. User Input:  front and back registration
Ground Truth: ### Front-to-Back (FTB) Registration\n\nFront-to-back registration is crucial for ensuring that the images on the front and back sides of a printed sheet align correctly. Here are the steps and considerations for troubleshooting and ensuring accurate front-to-back registration:\n\n1. **Check Registration Marks**:\n   - For every FTB printed sheet, check against the light if the crop/registration marks on the back side of the sheet match those printed on the front side.\n   - They should be located within a 0.4mm radius (0.8mm diameter) area around the crop/registration marks on the front side of the sheet ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/20009), page 19).\n\n2. **Image Placement Accuracy**:\n   - Print 12 sheets of a/the CATP job.\n   - Discard the first two printed sheets and start checking from the third printed sheet.\n   - Measure the crop/registration marks spread (FTF/FTB) on the printed substrate and ensure it is within spec ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/20009), page 17).\n\n3. **Adjustments for Registration Problems**:\n   - Use image placement settings on the Press Controller to fix registration problems between the image placement and imposition on the front and back side of the substrate for a given job.\n   - The operator will usually move the back image to match the front and ensure both sides are centered ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29648), page 12).\n\n4. **Checking and Adjusting Registration**:\n   - Print 500 duplex copies of a CATP job with eye-marks.\n   - Check every 50 copies for front-to-back tolerance of +/- 250 microns.\n   - If adjustment is needed, navigate to Main Menu > Substrate > Web Handling System > Front to back.\n     - For vertical registration, change the value by the eye mark distance to nip on Engine 2.\n     - For horizontal registration, change the Web Guide value on Engine 2 ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/21536), page 129).\n\n### Sources:\n1. **Front-to-Back (FTB) Troubleshooting**:\n   - Document: Front-to-Back (FTB) Troubleshooting\n   - Author: HP Indigo\n   - Link: [https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/20009](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/20009)\n   - Page: 17, 19\n\n2. **HP SmartStream, Production Pro Print Server - Direct2Finish, User Guide**:\n   - Document: HP SmartStream, Production Pro Print Server - Direct2Finish, User Guide\n   - Author: HP Indigo\n   - Link: [https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29648](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/29648)\n   - Page: 12\n\n3. **HP Indigo W7200 Digital Press Installation Manual**:\n   - Document: HP Indigo W7200 Digital Press Installation Manual\n   - Author: HP Indigo\n   - Link: [https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/21536](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/21536)\n   - Page: 129

Front -to-Back (FTB)  Troubleshooting Document  \nCA393 -03380  Rev 06  17 \n Image placement accuracy  \nThis section provides information regarding FTF (front -to-front) and FTB  (front -to-back) graphical \nspecs on HP Indigo 7000 Series Digital Presses.  \nProcedure:  \n1. Print 12 sheets of a/the CATP job.  \n2. Throw away the first two printed sheets and start checking from the third printed sheet.  \n3. Measure the crop/registration marks spread (FTF / FTB) on the printed substrate and make sure \nit is in spec . \nNOTE : Refer to the sections below and to the figures in the Appendix - Image placement \naccuracy spec . \nSame sid e stability (FTF –  simplex)  \nMeasure the variation of sheet -to-sheet (FTF) image placement.  \n1. Measure the location of the crop/registration marks on the third sheet and note it down. This \nwill serve as your reference.  \n2. For each printed  sheet after the third one, check that the position of every crop/registration \nmark matches that of the corresponding mark on the third (reference) sheet.  \nThe crop/registration marks should be positioned within a  0.2mm radius  (0.4mm diameter ) \narea around the corresponding mark on the third (reference) sheet.  \n3. If the FTF is not in spec, refer to the relevant troubleshooting section in this document.  \nOpposite sides registration (FTB – duplex)  \nMeasure the shift of the front -to-back (FTB) image placement .  \n1. On every FTB printed sheet, check against the light if the crop/registration marks on the back side of the sheet match those printed on the front side, or are at least located within a  0.4mm \nradius  (0.8mm diameter) area around the crop/registration marks o n the  front sheet.  \n2. If the FTB is not in spec, refer to the relevant troubleshooting section in this document.'), Document(metadata={'ratingResponse': {'number_of_votes': 0, 'rating': 0.0}, 'persona': 'Engineer', 'format': 'pdf', 'description': 'To describe how to install the HP Indigo W7200 Digital Press. Image placement\nAs part of the initial DFE setup for Finishing, you can make specific  adjustments to the image placement settings \non the Press Controller .\nThere are a number of use cases in which these adjustments can be helpful or necessary. The following are just \na few examples.\nUse Cases\n● Registration problems : Use image placement to fix registration problems between the image placement \nand imposition on the front and back side of the substrate for a given job.\n– The operator will usually move the back image to match the front.\n– The operator needs to make sure that both the front and back sides are centered. The side that is not \ncentered will be shifted to match the other side.\n– In this case, there is no need to modify the JDF . The AddPressImagePlacement  check box in the DFE \nneeds to be unchecked.\n● Blanket defects : Use image placement to move the entire image to avoid a scratch or other defect on the \nblanket.\n– The operator will need to move both sides (front and back) using the same values for each.\n– The JDF must reflect  the change in position. Therefore, the AddPressImagePlacement  check box in \nthe DFE must be checked.\n– All four of the ImagePlacementShift  values should be set to 0.\n● Registration problems  and Blanket defects : Use image placement to adjust for both registration problems \nand blanket defects.\n– In this case, the operator needs to enter a value in the IPC configuration  that reflects  the values set \nthat will affect  the JDF .\n– Example : There is a front (side A) to back (side B) misregistration. The back side is shifted in 3 mm \n(0.12 in) and the image should be moved 5 mm (0.2 in) to avoid a scratch on the blanket.\nFigure 2-9  Image placement problems illustration\n8 Chapter 2   Setup procedures ENWW')]

User Input:  ILP
Ground Truth: The term \'ILP\' refers to the Inline Primer used in HP Indigo digital presses. Here are some key points and steps related to ILP from the documents:\n\n1. **Installation of ILP on HP Indigo 6K Digital Press**:\n   - Place the parallel jig on the left ILP bridge roller and ILP roller.\n   - Adjust the screw behind the ILP roller to ensure parallelism.\n   - Recheck the parallelism and level of the ILP and all ILP bridge rollers.\n   - Connect the unwinder bridge to the ILP by moving it close to the ILP ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/52556), page 83).\n\n2. **Service and Troubleshooting of ILP**:\n   - Verify the sealing of the inside of the ILP exhaust system at the blower connection.\n   - For newer ILP configurations with exhaust hose assembled, follow specific steps to service the ILP exhaust system ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335), page 91).\n   - For older ILP configurations without exhaust hose assembled, ensure the entire ILP exhaust system is properly sealed and verify the implementation of Service Note CA392-02581 ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335), page 88).\n   - Secure the ILP exhaust from the top and inside using all the screws provided.\n   - Service the ILP blower yellow belt by verifying the implementation of the blower belt Service Note and identifying the correct belt size ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335), page 93).\n   - Remove the ILP encoder by disconnecting the ILP encoder connector and using a small Phillips screwdriver to remove the screw ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335), page 129).\n\n### Sources:\n1. HP Indigo 6K Digital Press Installation, CA393-11140, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/52556), page 83.\n2. ILP Service and Troubleshooting, CA393-05680, [source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/27335), pages 88, 91, 93, 129.

User Input:  reinsertion
Ground Truth: ### Reinsertion Assembly Servicing and Installation\n\n#### Servicing the Reinsertion Assembly\n\n1. **Remove the Metal Cable Sheath:**\n   - Unscrew and remove the metal cable sheath from the side of the reinsertion sensor control ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/23240), page 18).\n\n2. **Remove the Reinsertion Assembly:**\n   - Remove the four Allen M6 screws, washers, and spring washers securing the reinsertion assembly to the feed unit rear wall.\n   - Remove the reinsertion assembly from the press and save the screws, washers, and spring washers ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/23240), page 18).\n\n3. **Remove the Reinsertion Motor:**\n   - Remove the four screws securing the reinsertion motor.\n   - Disconnect the wiring from the bracket ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/23240), page 19).\n\n4. **Install the New Reinsertion Motor:**\n   - Install the new reinsertion motor in the reinsertion assembly.\n   - Reinstall the reinsertion assembly in the press.\n   - Mount and connect the cable sheath to the side of the reinsertion sensor control ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/23240), page 19).\n\n#### Installing New Sync Reinsertion Sensor\n\n1. **For New Press Installation:**\n   - Use the new reinsertion common assembly supplied in kit CA390-10421.\n   - Insert the 4 hex screws to attach the assembly to the rear wall ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/188422), page 15).\n\n2. **For Replacing an Existing Sensor:**\n   - Reinstall the reinsertion common assembly that was removed in the previous steps.\n   - The replacement kit does not include a new unit ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/188422), page 15).\n\n3. **Connecting the Assembly:**\n   - After connecting the assembly to the press, run the fiber optic cables to the rear side of the engine ([source](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/188422), page 15).\n\n### Sources\n1. **Web Handling System (WHS) in the Printing Engine**\n   - Author: HP Indigo\n   - Link: [Web Handling System (WHS) in the Printing Engine](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/23240)\n   - Pages: 18-19\n\n2. **Installing New Sync Reinsertion Sensor - 8K**\n   - Author: HP Indigo\n   - Link: [Installing New Sync Reinsertion Sensor - 8K](https://www.printos.com/knowledge-zone/#/view/asset/188422)\n   - Pages: 2, 10, 15
